--- 帖子 #1 ---
Hi everyone,

When I released Roadmap ( https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...o-read-markets ), I was conscious that it was a strategy which required a fair amount of discretion/judgement.

I still receive many messages from people who are successfully trading using Roadmap, which is great. However, I wanted to also provide one of my other strategies for those who might prefer a more rules-based approach.

Welcome to Daylight.

This is a strategy with clear entry rules, various exit options and no non-standard indicators. I will walk you through how to set up your charts and will provide a template for those who want it.

But first, here's a look at a typical chart.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

As you can tell from the chart above, we are using Williams %R but we are using it in a non-standard way. We are actually hiding the normal line and instead applying a Smoothed 8 period MA and a Smoothed 21 period MA to the data.

Additionally, on our main chart, we have a 5 period Smoothed MA and another 5 period Smoothed MA with a shift of 5.

And that's all you will need to get started.

Attached below is a template and in my next posts I will fully explain the strategy, with entry criteria and exit options. I've also attached a link to my Journal, which contains some posts you may find generally useful.

https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...just-a-journal

--- 帖子 #2 ---
Let's look again at the chart I posted previously, but this time with some entry arrows added.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

We get a short entry signal when the following rules are met:

1. Red MA above Green MA on main chart and daylight exists between them.

2. Price closes below Green MA on main chart.

3. Red MA above Blue MA in sub-window and daylight exists between them.

Vice versa for long entry signals.

As you can see from the chart, we had two short winners and one long loser. Also notice the period leading up to the first entry. There was no daylight between the red and green MAs and very little daylight between the red and blue MAs. This is what attempts to keep us out of sideways markets.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

In the above chart we have 5 entries, with 1 loser, 3 winners and 1 trade in progress.

When it comes to exits, you have various options. You can either:

1. Exit when the red and blue MAs both start to slope in the opposite direction in the sub-window.

2. Exit when the red and green MAs cross again.

3. Exit when the red and blue MAs cross again.

4. Exit when you reach a set profit target (for example, a percentage of ADR or a multiple of ATR).

Each option has advantages and disadvantages so you should establish which suits your trading personality and risk profile. Some of you will prefer to let a trade breathe to catch the occasional big runner, others will prefer to extract smaller profits more regularly.

In terms of stop losses, I take the same approach with this strategy as I do with Roadmap. I do not believe in being taken out by a stop loss. Instead I look to exit manually when I am proven wrong. In this case, any of the exit criteria above could be used to be a sign of being proved wrong.

However, that's not to say we should trade without stops. I believe in emergency stops far away from price. They simply exist as a fall-back if something major happens or if I unexpectedly have to leave my screen for a period of time.

There is also the option of adding to a winner if you want to stack trades. This approach won't be for everyone so I won't go into too much detail now but essentially you are looking to add when you are a certain number of pips/points ahead with the aim of capitalising on a trend you have found yourself in.

I have deliberately posted 15 minute charts as I believe they should be the smallest timeframe you trade this strategy on. You are welcome to try lower timeframes but be warned that the noise will likely reduce your profitability. Higher timeframes should be fine however, if this suits you better.

*Edit* - Indices can be traded profitably on 5m timeframe.

I also deliberately chose the thickness of the lines for the sub-window MAs. This is important when you consider that daylight between thinner or thicker lines would be different.

I don't really trade Forex much these days as I prefer to trade indices, gold or oil. But if you are a Forex trader, you need to be aware of when news is due that could impact the pair you are trading. I would advise being flat before major news if at all possible.

So, there you have it.

That is Daylight.

I will try to post lots of live examples in this thread over the coming weeks but please do feel free to ask if you have any queries in the meantime.

Hi,

It certainly can be used on the daily timeframe. It probably requires smaller size or quicker exits though, to account for the larger swings.

I've attached a couple of daily charts with examples:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

On the above Dow chart I've marked a couple of potential entry points but you could have entered almost anywhere in that up trend and profited well. Also notice how the dip resulted in a cross of the sub-window MAs but there wasn't any daylight between them. This stops you from taking a counter-trend short.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

On EURUSD I've marked a few potential entry points. Again though, you could in theory have entered in multiple places for multiple trades if you wished. Notice again how the dip resulted in the sub-window MAs converging but no daylight forming between them.

--- 帖子 #41 ---
Hi,

In numerical terms, the difference between the 8 SMMA and 21 SMMA should be around 4 or more. That should allow just enough daylight to avoid lots of false signals and hopefully also allow you good entries.

The way the strategy is designed, it will usually miss the start of a trend. This is deliberate as we want a bit of confirmation that a direction change is happening before we enter.

For forex I prefer to stick to 15m+ but you can certainly try 5m and see how it goes. If you do, please let us know. In terms of multi-timeframe analysis, none is required. Best to take the signals based on the timeframe you are trading.

I don't subscribe to the Risk Reward model. A positive RR can result in a losing strategy in the same way as a negative RR can result in a winning strategy. What I view as more important is win rate, average win amount, average loss amount and profit factor.

In terms of how and where I take profit, it's based on various elements. Market structure, amount of profit relative to ADR etc etc. Every trade is unique in that respect.

--- 帖子 #46 ---
Thanks for your kind words. I'm glad things make sense so far.

I wouldn't be inclined to use Roadmap and Daylight together. I guess there might be some hybrid approach that works fine but they are very different in terms of criteria and, as you say, it could lead to confusion due to information overload.

However, you could make use of key information from Roadmap to assist your decision making. For example, if an instrument is at ADR High, you would want to avoid taking long Daylight signals. Fortunately that's quite easy to do by adding the relevant Roadmap indicators to your chart.

--- 帖子 #59 ---
Daylight Tradingview Version:https://www.tradingview.com/script/p...pbfx-Daylight/ https://www.tradingview.com/script/v...fx-Williams-R/
Description:

This is the bundle of the indicators used by the amazing LauraT over at FF using her *new* method call Daylight Trading Strategy, just like her previous strategy, this one is even more minimalist and rule-based trend following / continuation of trend, more information on her forum thread.

FEATURES:

- 2 Smoothed Simple Moving Average applied to a default Williams %R data

- 2 Smoothed Simple Moving Average of 5-Period (1 been offset to 5 periods forward) where user uses price reaction at line crosses to make trading decisions

EXTRAS:

- 200-Period Simple Moving Average the pillar of this setup where dictates trend movement;

- 8-Period High/Low Channel EMA following the price close for fast changing in trade direction;

- 14-Period ADR High/Low with reactive lines that signals when price has exceeded the ADR limit;

- Previous Day High/Low levels which serves as Support/Resistance;

- Daily Open line plot on the chart where price sometimes try to go back to before changing direction;

- Trading Session Highlight, this is defaulted at London/New York sessions (can be edited) to make a better visual representation of when the best volatile hours are in play (this is not a calculation of volatility, is just the time of day based on market availability)

--- 帖子 #68 ---
Apologies, wasn't at my desk for a few hours.

There are various things I consider when deciding whether to take an entry but these don't necessarily mean I avoid all the bad trades and take all the good ones  Sometimes the perfect setup will present itself and then will not work out. That's trading.

I'll go into more detail about this later but, for now, here are some initial ideas of things to be wary of:

1. Be careful when entering where price has already moved quite far from the green line. Chances are high for a retracement. Better to wait a little and enter on the retracement.

2. Be wary of entering when blue line is starting to slope down as this could easily turn into a reversal. Better to wait for the line to flatten out.

3. When the green and red lines have been intertwining for a while, with green on top then red then green etc etc, it's usually best to find a different opportunity.

--- 帖子 #69 ---

--- 帖子 #70 ---
Hi,

Yes, perfectly fine to enter on those candles. In fact, it's often better to enter after a retracement (as long as other conditions still valid) as you will be getting in at a much better price.

--- 帖子 #80 ---
Aggressive Hourly Option

I was going to avoid mentioning this until later in the thread but I'm conscious that some people might want more aggressive entries. Here's an option for you.

I would advise you trade this style on the hourly charts only. I haven't tested it on other timeframes and I have a feeling it won't perform as well on them. Shorter will contain too much noise and longer will involve massive swings in capital.

We still use a 5 period smoothed moving average on the main chart but this time we have two of them. One is set to the High and the other is set to the Low. This creates a channel, which will be familiar to Roadmap traders.

In the sub-window, we change the smoothed moving averages to 5 and 13.

Let's look at some examples on a chart and I'll talk you through how to trade it.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

We first look for a signal bar on the main chart. A signal bar is one that either closes above (for longs) or below (for shorts) the channel. Starting from the left, our signal bar is marked with an arrow. However, we don't yet have daylight in the sub-window. We need to have that before we have an entry. That arrives two bars later and we can enter short. The trade progresses very well indeed.

Then we get an opposite signal when price closes above the channel. This time daylight exists in the sub-window and we can enter long immediately. Again, the trade progresses very well. Notice what happens later in the move though. The sub-window moving averages cross to the downside. However, there is no signal bar as price fails to close below the channel. If we are still in our long at this point, we can stay in.

Let's look at a messier example.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Here we see a signal bar and, two bars later, we get our daylight so we can enter long. The trade doesn't work out and we exit either when the bar closes below the channel or on the next bar, when the sub-window averages cross. That bar also gives us a short entry as both signal and daylight are in place. The short initially progresses well but notice that a bar eventually closes above the channel. However, this does not have to be an exit signal. It can be if you prefer, but it doesn't have to be. Because the sub-window averages do not cross.

I hope this makes sense but, as always, please feel free to ask questions if you have any.

I've also attached a template for this alternative approach.

Greetings LauraT.....

This is the way I have been trading for the past 2 years now......

5 SSMA - high.

5 SSMA - low.

Timeframe - H1 or M30.

After the signal candle that break/close above/below the channels.....I normally wait for the next candle to close above/below the signal candle and this second candle must not touch the channel.....so my entry candle is the next candle....which is the third candle.

Happy trading

Here's a long I took on a much higher timeframe (H4).

Wanted to highlight this trade as it demonstrates another way to play the strategy. Instead of entering as soon as I had daylight, I waited for a retracement back to the green line.

With this approach, the risk will always be that it reverses and the opportunity is gone. But the upside is that you will get in at a 'better' price and, if it does reverse, your loss will be smaller.

--- 帖子 #155 ---
UC long - standard mode - 5m.

Something to note here - when a strong trend is persisting, the red moving average in the sub-window will stay on one side of the Williams % -50 line.

For those who want to be extra cautious and only enter on the side of the prevailing trend, this could be an additional filter. It will mean less entries (or later entries in some cases) but will help you avoid fighting a strong trend.

Notice how both short signals failed as the up trend was strong.

Edit - This refers to standard mode only. It will not be a reliable filter in aggressive mode due to the shorter MA.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #164 ---
First, add a 14 period Williams %R and set the colour to 'none' (we want to hide that line).

Next, drag a Moving Average onto the Williams %R window and set to Smoothed 21 coloured red with a line thickness of the 3rd option and set 'applied to' as First Indicator Data.

Finally, drag another Moving Average onto the Williams %R window and set to Smoothed 8 coloured blue with a line thickness of the 3rd option and set 'applied to' as First Indicator Data.

--- 帖子 #169 ---
Thank you.

Others might take an approach based on RRR but I don't believe it is optimal. I'll explain.

If I offered you a strategy where you were risking 20 pips to win 5 you wouldn't want it based on RRR. But RRR by itself is meaningless. That same strategy that many would instantly turn down has a win rate of 97%. Suddenly the RRR doesn't seem so bad, right?

Personally, I track the following stats:

1. Win rate.

2. Average Loss (in monetary terms).

3. Average Win (in monetary terms).

4. Profit Factor (Total monetary gain divided by total monetary loss).

Apologies if any of this is me stating the obvious, but I see a lot of focus on RRR at the expense of more meaningful statistics so perhaps this will help someone.

In terms of your specific question though (about taking profit), I find market conditions these days to be more amenable for taking small and regular profits rather than going for big runners. One approach you might find helpful is to aim for a percentage of Average Daily Range. So, if ADR is 100, you might decide to take profits in chunks of 20 pips. And, if there happens to be a strong continuous trend where it goes 100 pips in one direction, there is nothing stopping you from jumping in and out of that trend, banking 20 pips 3 or 4 times.

Here's a EURUSD chart that shows what has happened to volatility since last summer:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

It is almost half of what it was. So we adapt to market conditions and take smaller chunks of profit more regularly. Or, alternatively, we target 10 pips instead of 20 and double our size.

--- 帖子 #172 ---
helene1, all the indicators are in the template... daylight.tmp----- that Laura uploaded in the post #1, here https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...ading-strategy

Download that file {template) to a place where you can find it later...

Open Metatrader

Go to FILE --->>>NEW chart [any or favorite]

Now go to the "template" tab, looks like a little window, click the little arrow at the right, click "load template, and go to the folder or place where you saved the daylight template from post #1, click it and presto.. you got the full system in you terminal.

Note.. the Williams Indicator HAS NOT any adjustable parameter, I mean first indicator data, etc, install it, just choose period 14, color NONE, and then go to the navigator [indicators], looks like a yellow star, click it, and at the top, under trend,  choose moving average, click it and at the same time hold the mouse button down, drag it to the window where the Williams are, release the mouse button and now you can choose in-->> APPLY to....FIRST Indicator DATA [the WPR was first, right?], the parameters, [21 or 8 or...] now drag the second moving average, input parameters {only if you aren't using the template, and thats it

Hope this helps

--- 帖子 #175 ---
Whether you're using the standard version or aggressive version, and regardless of which timeframe you are trading, I want to take a moment to highlight the importance of daylight existing in the sub-window.

During any move, there will be 'shake-outs' - counter moves designed to shake market participants (who have chosen the direction correctly) out of their positions. Daylight won't be able to eradicate those shake-outs completely, but it certainly can help.

Below I've marked up some charts where participants would possibly have been shaken out of positions. Notice how there was no daylight in the sub-window. Waiting for daylight would have kept you on the correct side.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Hi,

This strategy is one I actually used years ago with good results but I moved on to design something else once I got attracted to shorter timescale trading (I originally only used Daylight on 15m timeframe).

Recently I decided to dig it out and check if it still works. As we know, market conditions change and what worked once might not work now. Thankfully, it still performed well.

Since I've been able to take a look at it with fresh eyes (and more experience under my belt) I have seen the potential for slightly different approaches. Hence the aggressive version. The basic framework is such that it's quite straightforward to make small amendments and provide traders with more than one option.

I will continue my research, using different timescales etc, but so far I'm comfortable that both the original version and the aggressive version are suitable for a few timescales.

--- 帖子 #184 ---
I want to use yesterday's action on GU to highlight why shorter timeframes can be tricky. I know a lot of people are drawn to 1m or 5m charts but hopefully these examples will show why it's sometimes optimal to stick to 15m at lowest.

Let's first look at the 15m charts for both standard and aggressive modes:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

As you can see, it wouldn't have mattered whether you chose standard or aggressive as both would have rewarded you with around 40 pips profit during the London session.

Now let's look at the same period of time on 5m charts, both standard and aggressive:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Much trickier, right?

I completely understand the desire to trade short timeframes and, for certain faster moving instruments, it can be lucrative. But, for the majority of currencies, I find that Daylight generally performs best when using 15m at lowest.

That's not to say 5m doesn't occasionally have its place with currencies though. Some days the trends and reversals will be such that 5m captures the moves perfectly. But other days it will drag you in and out of positions that result in frustrating small wins or losses.

The thing to keep in mind about Daylight is that it thrives during trends. An instrument will generally display trending behaviour on at least one timeframe. The key is finding that timeframe and trading it.

Pay close attention to the picture i have made. Study all details especially how Williams % top and bottom for swing high and low. Manualy make a line top and bottom for the average of Williams%. This is your swing high and low.

Trade only in the trend direction (Black Line) Yellow line is very important and is used in multiple ways. StochRSI is the trigger and must meet in line with Yellow line. Converge in the trend direction, Bump the same as pullback.

Back test your self before using this strategy, and watch the behaviour of yellow line ( Williams%)  Study every scenario. And remember every pair is different.

Price action and liquidity is giving you the clues. The strategy is the confirmation.

--- 帖子 #190 ---
Depends on the instrument (and to some degree current market conditions).

For example, I'd recommend not trading currencies on anything lower than 15m most of the time. However, there are times when a 5m currency chart will offer advantages in terms of speed of signals. In heavily trending days especially. But yes, overall, 5m will mostly lead to frustration.

When it comes to trading indices, oil or gold though, 5m can work pretty well.

Often it's best to look at what came before. I usually start with a 15m chart and work from there. I look at the last day or so of price action and make a judgement on whether I can trade that type of action if it repeats. I guess with experience you learn whether to go up or down a timeframe.

--- 帖子 #193 ---
Your chart reminds me of a point I haven't made yet.

There will be times in aggressive mode, as in your highlighted area, where daylight occurs before we get price closing on the correct side of the channel.

It's perfectly fine to take a chance on entering before the bar closes if it seems fairly obvious the bar is going to close on the correct side. In your example, we got the huge bar up on the hourly. Had we taken a chance and entered 15 minutes before the bar closed, we would have got in at 8 pips lower than waiting for the hourly bar to close. 8 pips won't seem like much of a payoff for taking a chance early but over the course of a week or month of trading it will add up to something worthwhile.

To be clear though, I'm only referring to cases where it seems fairly obvious the bar is going to close on the correct side of the channel. I definitely don't advise gambling on a marginal bar that could still close either side.

I previously mentioned using the -50 WPR line to form a bias. Here are a couple of examples from the 4H timeframe (a timeframe I'm finding remarkably lucrative in tests).

Oil first:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

We get in when there is both daylight and the 21 SMMA is above the -50 line. We get out when there is negative daylight, for a total profit of 380 points.

Dow next:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

We get in when there is both daylight and the 21 SMMA is above the -50 line. If we get out when there is negative daylight, we bank a profit of 613 points. The peak profit was actually over 1000 points if you had exited by some other means.

This is a trade that is slightly different to what I've posted so far. I wanted to fade weakness in the hope that the trend would re-assert itself. The red MA in the sub-window was staying above -50 and I took my bias from that. I waited until price was in the middle of the channel and the blue MA in the sub-window dipped below the red MA.

Taking this approach can help ensure you get in at a better price than taking the entry as soon as you get a buy signal.

--- 帖子 #303 ---
Tradingview Code :

//@version=3

study(title = "Shift Smoothed Moving Average", shorttitle="Sh_SMMA", overlay=true)

len1 = input(5, minval=1, title="Length")

src1 = input(close, title="Source")

smma1 = 0.0

smma1 := na(smma1[1]) ? sma(src1, len1) : (smma1[1] * (len1 - 1) + src1) / len1

plot(smma1, color=lime, linewidth=3)

shift_length = input(5, title="Shift")

len2 = input(5, minval=1, title="Length")

src2 = input(close, title="Source")

smma2 = 0.0

smma2 := na(smma2[1]) ? sma(src2, len2) : (smma2[1] * (len2 - 1) + src2) / len2

plot(smma2, color=orange,offset=shift_length, linewidth=3)

--- 帖子 #309 ---
Further to my previous post, I can now set out the strategy for purely trading the cross of the -50 line by the slow moving average.

The first decision we have to make is whether to use aggressive or standard mode. There are pros and cons to each. The standard mode will get you into positions later but will have less false signals, whereas the aggressive mode will get you in earlier but has more false signals. Personally, I prefer aggressive mode but the choice is yours.

The next decision is how much, if at all, of a buffer you want to use. I would recommend you have a buffer if using aggressive mode as it will help to reduce false signals. I'm using a buffer of 3 right now. That means that I will not get a long signal until the slow moving average goes above -47 (and below -53 for a short signal).

Next you need to establish a position/money management strategy. I recommend, if possible, splitting your entry in 3. Aim to take one third off at the first TP level, one third at the second TP level and final third at the point of the crossover. So, using Dow as an example, I might take one third off at +30, another third at +50 and the final third at the point of the crossover. You will need to come up with an appropriate figure for each individual instrument you trade. I appreciate that some of you might be trading micro lots and therefore be unable to split your position in 3. If that is the case, I recommend taking regular profit and re-entering. So, if trading EU for example, you might decide to take profit every 10 pips. This isn't ideal compared to splitting a position in 3 but it's probably the best workaround available to you.

Let's look at a live example:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

You can see our entry point marked by the magenta arrow. The trade is currently up around 70 points since our entry. We'd have taken off the first third at +30 and the second third at +50 so we'd currently have one third left running.

Another example:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Here we see a short entry on Gold on Friday. This would have been worth around 150 points if you held until end of play Friday (even more if you held over the weekend). Again, I'd recommend taking off your position in one thirds. So for Gold we might take off our first third at +40, second third at +70 and final third at end of the trading day for +150. That would give us around 87 points profit in total (+260 divided by 3).

Have a play around the the indicator and settings on different markets. Work out a plan based on the volatility of the instrument. This will be highly profitable in the right conditions.

As requested, I've included a template for aggressive mode.

Attached File(s)   !!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!Daylight50.tpl

In April 2015 I had an Aortic Aneurysm that ruptured and I ended up with a 14 hr emergency open heart surgery. During the surgery, I had a stroke that affected my memory among other things. One of the things that I would advise is to not focus on the money....instead focus on execution. Laura has given you a trading guide, now it is your responsibility to implement it. Focus on making sound trading decisions and review your trades to make sure that you followed your plan. We don't know where the market will go so we must have plans for any movement after we enter. Develop your plan and then trade it!

My signature sums this all up.......PLAN...PREPARE...EXECUTE....REPEAT

--- 帖子 #342 ---
Hi,

Yes, H4 should be fine as a trend indicator for M15.

When it comes to entries, sometimes it's best to wait for a retracement but other times it just keeps going and doesn't retrace. So unfortunately there isn't a hard and fast rule you can apply. It's a matter of judgement. One 'rule' you can use for yourself though is to not enter on massive bars that have extended too far from the MAs on the main chart. Big moves like that tend to retrace more.

--- 帖子 #387 ---
Yes,I saw it,this would be the next candle that went inside the channel. Does a retracement entry consists one in which price retraces inside the channel without candle closing within that area?

--- 帖子 #388 ---
It can be any variety really. It can be one that closes inside the channel or one where price temporarily goes inside the channel or gets close to it.

The general idea is that, if price travels too far away from the channel, you try to wait for a better price. Of course, the risk then becomes that the market just keeps going and going and you never get an entry.

--- 帖子 #389 ---
It's acceptable taking a loss even when price goes to the wrong side of the channel and never returns,the risk is much lower,just as your example where price travels too far away from the channel and getting in there.Sometimes the trend is very strong and retracements may well be less than 25% each time.....

Thank you again :-) Laura

--- 帖子 #390 ---
Yes, precisely. Waiting on the retrace opens you up to perhaps more risk of being on the wrong side of a reversal. But the flipside is the opportunity for a 'better' priced entry and a smaller loss if you are wrong.

--- 帖子 #394 ---
Hi,

No problem with your English.

Although I understand your reasoning for entering there, I think it's generally better to enter when momentum is in your favour. Most of the time, I'd prefer that the sub-window MAs be sloping downward for a short entry.

However, as you correctly identify, you were trying to get in on a retracement so you were likely well aware of the risk of a full reversal.

You were right not to exit at your line due to the MAs still being below -50. And you got the right result in the end - well done.

--- 帖子 #425 ---
This is the chart ADR indicator, 2 orange lines appear,when the ADR reaches max value for the day,you'll see bold thick RED lines compared to thin maybe dashed orange ones before,it simply means 100% ADR has been achieved for the day on a given instrument.....some traders use this as support and resistance,like a zone for retracement or trend continuation.....mainly an ''area of value''.

Eg: GBPUSD just crossed 100% ADR for today,those ADR lines should be RED Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #447 ---
Well, it's not a trading method per se, it's a tool used to show where price may go on a normal volatility day.

As you can see, there have been some 200% range days, but knowing volatility has increased, you would put the take profits further away

What else or how else do you determine where price might go and stop, consolidate, etc?

This is why support and resistance work sometimes, price only moves so much on a daily basis, and those levels have to line up at some point.

To answer your question, yes, it works for me, I have taken profit at times when the price had moved 1 x ADR.

Good luck

--- 帖子 #458 ---
Hi Laura, for Barraka WPR, what did you set for:

1. Use -50 level as filter

2. Display only mid-line crosses

Aren't they the same meaning?

Thank you.

--- 帖子 #459 ---
Hi,

It's not highlighted because when the MAs on the chart did not respect the rules (green above red) when the Williams cross happened.

It's actually a pretty rare occurrence, because the vast majority of the time when the Williams daylight happens, the chart MAs are already in the correct order.

The arrows / signals are displayed only on the WPR cross, so when finally the chart moving averages did cross, it doesn't trigger an arrow.

However the dashboard that I have provided does signal a chart cross, so you could always use that if you want.

--- 帖子 #460 ---
No, they are not the same thing:

- Use -50 as filter: only displays signals (whether standard or aggro) when the WPR cross takes place on the correct side of the midline. So, for a bull signal for example, the WPR red & blue need to be above the midline. And inverse for a sell signal.

- Display only midline crosses: This is a variation of daylight that Laura explained later on in the thread. The rules are different, and it's basically taking signals when the slow WPR (red) crosses the midline (-50) level. When you choose that option, there is no "daylight" involved, it's just a midline cross.

--- 帖子 #465 ---
Hi,

With any timeframe, you have to do a little visual testing on various markets to see what works best.

Timeframes other than 15m are still relatively newly explored by me so I can't yet say I favour one approach over the other. By giving what I consider to be a solid set of options, I'm providing a starting point for people to go on and do their own research. Nobody should take my word for anything without testing it out themselves.

A key point to remember is this though. If market conditions are right on a particular timeframe, things will go very well indeed. If conditions are less ideal, it will be much trickier. That applies regardless of which approach or which timeframe is chosen. So the important thing isn't so much the approach or timeframe, but the state of the instrument at the time you trade. Fortunately, we have many markets to choose from and we aren't forced to trade any in particular.

If you take a look at GU on the 4H for example - from mid-May to mid-June we were stuck in a range that would make extracting profit very difficult. As soon as we realise we are in such a range we avoid trading it and move on to find other opportunities.

--- 帖子 #466 ---
It's really a case of trying to establish, as soon as you can, that you are in a range and then either avoiding that market in favour of another or seeing if switching up to the Daily presents a clearer picture.

A trader might be caught out once or twice by a range but they shouldn't be repeatedly caught out. Once we realise what is happening, we avoid it like the plague until conditions change.

Try looking at the Daily and see if that seems preferable. If you can only trade the 4H, there has to be an acceptance that sometimes the best action will be not to trade a particular market.

--- 帖子 #467 ---
Yes -if your long fails and then your short fails, chances are you are in a range, so you mark the high and low and wait or get another instrument. Just my pennyworth.

--- 帖子 #470 ---
If you choose "Display only midline crosses" as true, it will only display midline crosses, regardless of the "-50 level filter" option.

If you set it to false, it will display normal signals. Those normal signals can be refined using the "-50 filter" option.

It's quite straightforward, really.

Better still, just place the indi on the chart, and play around with those 2 settings you'll immediately see what it relates to, by looking at where the arrows take place.

--- 帖子 #476 ---
Achal's post above reminds me to mention something.

We cannot, and should not, blindly follow every signal we get. Whether you use market structure, higher timeframe analysis or something else, the aim should always be to form a bias and wait for opportunities that agree with your bias.

No strategy will give you 'buy here' type signals that magically deliver profit every time. Daylight is no different in that respect.

All we can do is try to stack the probabilities in our favour. We do this by taking setups that we believe, over the long run, will deliver a profitable edge.

I hope, very soon, there will be an additional tool which will greatly assist in quickly performing this analysis. Until then, please do try to be aware of the bigger picture at all times.

If you were not using the -50 level as a filter, you could have taken the first short, and stuck to it until the breakout, and then taken a loss.

--- 帖子 #567 ---
Hi everybody. I'll post how I decide when to have a trade or not. I hope it can be useful for some of you. I don't want to modify Laura's setups, so it's just my way to use that amazing strategy. I've been testing it for just a week, so don't trade in real as it's something i'm improving.

Next, I add a GBPUSD graph for the last 3 days. I've marked 3 entry points, as you can see.  Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Why i did this 3 trades? That's easy. Just following Laura¡s rules but adding a currency strenght indicator (which I'll post later) that I use in order to confirm the trade. I look for a 3.0 points (at least, preferable 4.0) difference between the two involved currencies.

The second key is the MFI (15). In that case i don't have into consideration the 50 level. I look for divergence. If there's a divergence between the MFI and the price action i don't trade. As you can see, the three trades of GBPUSD are PERFECT, and a 20 pips can be reached easily. I don't recomend looking for more pips as I trade in H1, but the management of your trades are up to you, of course.

I put the SL at 30 pips, but i think 20 can be enough. Let's try it.

Now I show you another possible trade. AUDUSD Attached Image (click to enlarge)

As you can see, all is OK in order to open a trade for the next 1 or 2 hours. But, the MFI has a no clear direction, so I won't trade AUDUSD today. It's possible it can be a good entry, but I prefer just opening a trade when all is PERFECT.

For sure that can be improved. Open to listen!

--- 帖子 #570 ---
Just something quick that is MY opinion

-Trade in the direction of Price

-Use the channel as a "guide" for direction

-Use other side of channel to trail stop if you want....in your example there were several bars in your direction without even so much as a touch of the opposite channel line

-There is no such thing as  'perfect" trade because we simply DO NOT KNOW where price will go once we enter

- work on skills to manage your trades once entered instead of looking for ways to filter out the bad ones ( you will end up with your screen looking like a kids coloring book)

- Trying to avoid losing money is detrimental to your success because it is going to happen even with your very best efforts....learn to manage the losers

Look at your chart...I have marked a couple of lines (Big lines)  this is the direction of trade....follow the closed candles

--- 帖子 #571 ---
Hi everyone,

I notice that there is now a temptation to 'improve' or amend Daylight. This is human nature. We experience the discomfort of some losses and our subconscious tells us there must be a way to avoid taking a loss.

Be very wary of such thoughts.

I'm not going to say Daylight is perfect. No strategy is. But I think the most useful stage we can be at now is to start to discuss and highlight the nuances of what already exists. Not to add indicators or extra conditions but to understand the subtleties of trading this (or any) strategy.

In the same way that I gradually discussed those nuances with Roadmap, I will do so with Daylight. Because, the hard fact is, I could ask 100 people to trade the exact same strategy at the exact same times of day and get wildly different results. By understanding the nuances you will give yourself the best opportunity to have success.

So, I must respectfully request the following. If you want to add things, feel free. But please don't share these additions on this thread. It creates diversions that are unhelpful as people start going off in different directions. If, on the other hand, you notice subtle little elements of Daylight and want to share those observations - please do.

I will say more later (including some great news on an analysis tool!) but I wanted to address this topic before it got out of hand.

--- 帖子 #610 ---
What is a "loosing" trade?

--- 帖子 #611 ---
Open trade which is in a loss

--- 帖子 #612 ---
If you read Laura's journal you will find a section on management, plus the thread is dotted with discussion on management.

https://www.forexfactory.com/thread/...just-a-journal?

Note:

"Loosing" =
verb
gerund or present participle: loosing1.

set free; release.

"the hounds have been loosed"

Similar:

free, set free, unloose, turn loose, set loose, untie, unchain, unfasten

2. fire (a bullet, arrow, etc.).

"he loosed off a shot at the vehicle" Similar:

fire, discharge, shoot, eject, let go, let fly with.
Whereas "LOSING =

fail to win (a game or contest).

"England lost the first Test match"

Similar:

be defeated, be beaten, suffer defeat, be the loser, be conquered, be vanquished, fail ( "it was a losing trade) earn less (money) than one is spending or has spent.

"the paper is losing £1.5 million a month"

--- 帖子 #613 ---
Often confused with a "LOSING" trade

--- 帖子 #632 ---
Thank you Laura for sharing your knowledge with us. I have run a backtest on EURUSD and AUDNZD from 2019 to 2021.

Entry rule: enter when both W%R and the green and red moving averages agree. i.e. there is enough daylight between both pair of lines.

Exit when the green line crosses the red line on the other side.

Safety stop loss placed on a swing low/ swing high that is reasonable away from the entry.

Timeframe uses is the 4hr. Test bank was of 10,000.

Its early but by just taking mechanical trades and following the system's rules, it has returned a profit of 20% on EURUSD, while on AUDNZD it managed to move from a maximum drawdown of 6% to a closing profit of 9%.

The data used for back testing is from dukascopy using a fixed spread of 3 pips.

Of course there is no psychological factors during a backtest.

Hope this little test supports all the knowledge that you are sharing with us.

--- 帖子 #655 ---
Hi,

Good question. I'm unsure how useful posting my trades are as they are often quite straightforward and dull.

Part of the answer takes me back to Roadmap days and my Journal. I look at market structure primarily. In Daylight terms, I then look at the smoothed moving averages in the sub-window and see how they appear. In today's trades, I noticed that both market structure and the smoothed MAs were accommodative for further downside.

I tend to not trade currencies too often these days. I also tend to limit my active short-term trades to only two open at a single time. It means I can give them the required focus/management as I'm not having to look at too many markets.

Hope this helps.

so am i right in saying that we use the ADR to determine roughly the better pairs to trade on the day ? if so would someone be able to give a brief description on what to look for on the ADR please... thank you in advance

--- 帖子 #676 ---
Yes and No......Yes, ADR can be helpful in selecting the pair(s) to trade. We need volatility to trade. Yes, ADR can help with an intraday trade for exits and to make sure that there is room for the trade to move.  If a pair has used 90% of it's range already, probably not a lot left in it for the day.   Finally No, if you are trading larger timeframes, ADR does not matter as much I dont think because you will be in for several days and each days range is somewhat irrelevant as long as it is not "abnormal" like extremely large or small

--- 帖子 #700 ---
Hi Laura - thanks for an interesting strategy and to let you know that it is proving successful. I still have problems with Market Structure as this is discretionary! More on this if you can.

The way I have been trading is to look for an aggro signal (this example is a SELL) on say a 5 minute with the red/blue MA above the -50 : the blue has crossed under the red with daylight. Then check confluence on the next time frame - the Red/Blue should also be above the -50 and have been reasonably wide but the gap is starting to close - obviously there has not been an aggro signal on this time frame yet.

Have found this to be a good place to enter with half lots - then if price goes back into channel, add the other half.

Maybe I`m doing something wrong..but there are a lot of so called "false signals" when trying this strategy.

I only tried the 1Hour timeframe because I don`t like trading the noise on lower ones.

As a lot experienced traders say it is important to avoid unnessessery losses.

A good strategy should have a remarkable potential to filter out those angry thinngs.

I tried to add a 200sma as an additional filter and only trade in the direction of the main trend.

Then you will notice that you are going to miss some good opportunities in reverse direction and the win rate of this strategy will decrease immensely.

Should I try only higher timeframe like H4 or is this strategy only made for lower timeframes??

What are your methods to make your entries more safe or to avoid so called false signals?

The 200EMA is considered a key indicator by traders and market analysts for determining the overall long-term trend. The price level in a market that coincides with the 200EMA is recognized as a major support when price is above the 200EMA or resistance when price is below the 200EMA........so when the price is far away from the 200EMA you may still takes your trade.....even if opposite the main trend........and if price is very close to the 200EMA like less than 10pips......All you need to do is wait for the price to break the 200EMA.....once price has break it....... you're good to enter your trade.

This trading method is loving.......and combined Trend trading with Breakout trading to generate a decent opportunities on virtually all market conditions.

Therefore you're on course........look for trending market that's has a lot of strength and Momentum.

Happy weekend

--- 帖子 #733 ---
Baxter,

The 200EMA/200SMA are almost the same..... just choose one.

For your Strength and Momentum.......The Daylight is enough...... it's depends on the way you understand the trading signals.......

1. Strength.....both MA (blue and red lines) are above -50 for strong long.....and below -50 levels for strong short..... When both MA are above the -50 levels.....this means both the short-term trend and long-term trend are strong Long...... opposite for Short trade.

2. Momentum.....the wider the space between the two MA (blue and red lines) the better for momentum........you can never see me taking trades with a tiny Daylight........and watch out for big, bold candle that break the Channel above/below.

--- 帖子 #738 ---
Using Fast Moving Average To Enter Trends

Here is another way you can use the information contained on the charts to time entries. For these examples, I've used the hourly timeframe, a Smoothed 100 moving average and the aggressive settings. The principle should apply across timeframes and settings however.

When you decide you are in a directional trend (via the SMMA100, SMA200, MTF analysis, Barraka's dashboard or some other method), you wait for the fast moving average to travel to the 'wrong' side of the -50 line and back again. This provides your entry point. Below I've included some chart examples with manually added arrows to demonstrate those entry points.

No approach is perfect, and this is no exception, but for those struggling to pick a directional bias it might be of assistance. Please feel free to ask if any questions.

--- 帖子 #741 ---
This is the only pair I've tested over 5 years with a few rules to reduce losses. Each trade's risk is 1% of the capital that is approximately $100 risk per trade. Having carried out 275 trades the total return is of about 9% of the total investment (traded money not capital). If this result can be about the same on a good number of currency pairs, and assuming that about the same number of trades are taken on the other currency pairs. We can deduce that at least the number of trades taken will be 5x more. It is not much still, but the returns would have been 5x as much. Trading with a proprietary firm with a capital of 300K and banking half of 9% per year of the total traded money would be a nice extra money.

The trades where based on standard entries/system.

My rules for this test where:

Rule1:- R:R 1:1 (exits for me are a bit difficult to decide. If I had left the trades to run till the chart emas cross in the opposite direction I would have ridden some long trades but also lost more. This needs to be tested.)

Rule2:- Take a trade only when the candle closes on the green ema for long and vice versa for short. There must be daylight on both the W%R and the two chart emas. If there is no daylight on the %R wait up to 2 other candles from the first one that crossed the green ema. If there is no daylight on the close of the 3rd candle (counting the one after the cross) do not take the trade.

Rule3:- If the distance between the candle close and the green ema is larger than the 4hr ATR do not take the trade.

If anyone can suggest improvements on further test that I will take (when time permits) I would greatly appreciate it.

Again thank you Laura for sharing your success and inspiring us all.

Got the MQL4 book out and trying to add an alert to the MA cross indi. Doesnt seem to be working just yet. Any assistance would be appreciated. I copied the alert from another working indi. compiles ok but no alerts yet.

double range = iATR(NULL,0,10,i);

double maFast = iMA(NULL,0,FasterMA,0,MAMode,MAPrice1,i);

double maSlow1 = iMA(NULL,0,SlowerMA,2,MAMode,MAPrice2,i);

double maSlow2 = iMA(NULL,0,SlowerMA,2,MAMode,MAPrice3,i);

CrossUp[i] = EMPTY_VALUE;

CrossDown[i] = EMPTY_VALUE;

State[i] = State[i+1];

if (maFast>maSlow1) State[i] = 1;

if (maFast<maSlow2) State[i] = -1;

if (State[i] != State[i+1])

if (State[i] == 1)

{ CrossUp[i] = Low[i] -range/2.0;
if(i == 1 && Time[1] != time_alert) myAlert("indicator", "Buy"); //Alert on next bar open
time_alert = Time[1];

}

else {CrossDown[i] = High[i]+range/2.0;
if(i == 1 && Time[1] != time_alert) myAlert("indicator", "Sell"); //Alert on next bar open
time_alert = Time[1];

}}

return(0);

Dax short I took this morning. Wanted to highlight this trade to show that it's beneficial to have a degree of flexibility in relation to how we trade Daylight.

I was trading 5m Aggressive mode and you'll see from the chart that the fast moving average was above the slow moving average. However, the slow moving average was below -50. A lower high had been made and support had been broken. I expected price to want to test Friday's Low (dotted line).

There was a shakeout attempt, taking out that lower high but, crucially, the overnight structure was not broken. This convinced me to stick with my position. Eventually banked 59 points when it started to form a base below Friday's Low.

Although I've tried to ensure Daylight assists you with your entries and exits, there is no denying the fact that an appreciation of price action, market structure and the overall context of an instrument will deliver better profits (once proficient) than a mechanical approach will.

Hope this helps.

So based on your test, some of your assumptions are correct, but some are not. This is my opinion only and if you take it with a dollar bill to McDonalds you can get a cup of coffee.

Let me say first that your mechanical test is a really good first step. It gives you enough confidence in the bare bones of the system to spend more time working on learning the nuances of the system. Now, what should you do next? Why paper trade it of course (or very small lot if you like). You must demonstrate to yourself that you are capable of taking signals and adhering to the trading plan. (Discipline)

Once you can do these things to your satisfaction, you are ready to learn how to make money with this method.

Now, the reason some of your tests are not valid for me is that I simply would not take many of the trades that a mechanical system generates because of....wait for it.....Market Structure. This is where the rubber meets the road and the money is made. So what exactly are we talking about when I say market structure. Let me give you an example of a trade I am in and the decision process behind why I waited after the actual signal because of market structure.

I am short the EURCAD from a 4hr chart.

This first chart is the reason there have been no entries on this pair for a while......Sucker Soup
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

So why did I take this signal, but not when it first occurred.

This signal was just like the previous 7-10.....mixed in the soup...UNTIL it exited the green box to the downside with a sharp sell off.

I waited to see if it would retrace inside the channel, if not, oh well

I just so happens the top of the channel was in the same area as the bottom of the green box which should now act as resistance.

Yes, context is everything. Rules are there to be broken (in the right circumstances and when you fully realise why you are breaking them).  For example, I often trade the -50 line but I also love catching crossovers of the fast and slow when the fast is coming back from 'extreme' levels (-20/-80).

In terms of 4H trading, we do have Yesterday's High/Low. Those levels will always be relevant, regardless of timeframe used. But I do know what you mean about ADR. Although it's less visually appealing and less help as a timing tool, it can still be used on 4H charts to pinpoint the expected highs or lows.

There is another tool you might want to have a play with. I've attached it below. It calculates 3 probability highs and 3 probability lows based on ATR. You can define the time period the levels are valid for (daily, weekly etc). Unfortunately it doesn't have a history function, so the only way to check how accurate it might be is to forward test.

--- 帖子 #795 ---
I didn't get around to posting any trades during the day, sorry about that. However, I couldn't sleep tonight so thought I'd discuss a trade as people seem to want to know more about entries, trade management and exits.

The trade itself is nothing special but it does contain quite a few reference points that I think are worth highlighting. I've marked up the chart as follows:

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Let's start on the left hand side of the chart. We get a High followed by a Higher High. The trend is still up. The market then makes a Structure Low. By that, I mean the market sold off and then rejected the area and went higher. We now know this area is 'protected'.

As expected in an uptrend, the market confirms the direction by putting in a couple of Higher Lows. Now, the next part takes me back to something I mentioned in passing previously but it probably requires more emphasis so please excuse me for using bold text 'context is everything!' Keep in mind we are in a strong uptrend. What often happens at the end of a strong trend is the market goes from an orderly rise/decline to an exaggerated final push. Otherwise known as an Exhaustion Top or Exhaustion Bottom.

How do we know it's an Exhaustion Top in this case? Well, we don't. Not right away. But we gradually gather the clues. First, the most recent Higher Low is broken. Then we get a Lower High followed by another Lower Low. This should not happen in a healthy uptrend. So, we now believe the tide is turning and there might be a short opportunity. We should jump straight in! Well, no - we really shouldn't. Why? Because of our old friend the Structure Low. We need the market to test it and break it.

We do get the test (twice) of the Structure Low and third time is a charm as it breaks. Some people like to wait for a further re-test from below but I prefer not to risk missing the train so I get in straight away after the break. It then becomes a smooth ride down without much support. However, I was conscious of Yesterday's High sitting just below and realised it was possible the market would react and potentially bounce there.

I watched it closely at that level but it sailed right through, so I stayed in my position. I eventually decided it was time to bail out when I saw two things happening. The market went into a mini consolidation phase (lower highs and higher lows) and then broke that mini consolidation to the upside. That, together with the fact the low held firm, told me the party was over.

Notice that I've not even mentioned Daylight yet. Now let's take another quick look at the sub-window moving averages. The slow moving average went below -50 and the fast moving average stayed under the slow. Perfect conditions for shorting a market. But hopefully you see that, without context, the signal itself isn't enough.

Please let me know if this type of analysis is helpful or not. I'm happy to post a few more examples as the thread progresses if people find it useful.

--- 帖子 #822 ---
Hi,

I'm probably the worst person to answer this as my trade management style isn't very conventional

I don't use ATR for my TP or SL as I believe each market situation is unique. I try to take as much as I can from each move I participate in, with one eye on the exit door.

I also am not a fan of moving stops to breakeven. I believe we should try to get paid for every trade we take and I prefer to lock in a small profit. However, it's important not to do this too quickly as a trade should be given breathing room and a tight stop is just asking to be hit.

This is just my approach though, I'm sure others are different.

--- 帖子 #845 ---
Exits are the hardest part and require the most patience and discipline in my opinion.

I am actually using a couple of different exit methods.

First, I trail a stop above the top or below the bottom of the channel while I am away from the screen when it is moving in my direction.

I also use target area(s) for TP while I am not in front of my screen.

When I am in front of my screen, I watch price action around the same areas as my targets and manually exit.

I am now living in the USA so I am able to spend time usually 8-10 am EST and again for the Tokyo open from about 8-10pm EST

I enter most all of my trades during these timeframes.  I use the trailer overnight when I am asleep.

If I had to choose right now what I am finding to be the best for me, I would trail my stop above/below the other side of the channel and use selected targets that offer at least 2:1 RR or greater, preferably 3:1 or more.

--- 帖子 #848 ---
In addition, when I find a pair like this the first thing I do is to search other pairs from both sides of the trade. What I mean by this is that I start to look at all of the other AUD crosses for signs of setups on the 4hr timeframe. If I find others that have similar looks, I can assume that the AUD is a weak pair and I will look to add good shorts across the AUD complex.   I will then look at all CAD pairs for signs of strength just like I looked for weakness in the AUD.

Why do I do this? Because I want to pile on the weak currency short(s) across the board or vice versa, I want to be buying every setup across the board with the strong currency. If one was to look at all of the trades in the trading summary graphic I posted, you will that the vast majority money and winning trades were based off of two central themes....Strong Dollar and Strong Yen. When you do this, you are trading with the real true movement of currency in my opinion.

The other trades were really just one offs that were there and not part of any central "theme" so to speak.

Hope this makes sense.

--- 帖子 #854 ---
Ultimately it comes down to risk. If, as swingtrade sets out, a particular currency is firing off buy or sell signals across multiple pairs, that's a sign of a potential edge (and when our edge exists, we want to really push the boat out).

However, as i'm sure swingtrade would agree, we also have to maintain an overall risk profile we are comfortable with. For example, I wouldn't want to risk 1% on each of 6 USD shorts. That's simply too much risk associated with a single currency and an adverse move could do significant damage. But shorting a couple of Dollar pairs at the same time isn't in itself a problem.

I trade indices more than currencies now so, to apply the same principle, I can happily be long or short on two of the three indices I trade (Dow, Dax, Nasdaq) at any given time but never all 3 at once as the risk becomes too imbalanced for my liking.

--- 帖子 #855 ---
That's a tricky one as I no longer read 'trading' books.

I reached a point where I realised that the battle I was undertaking wasn't really against the market, but against myself. By that I mean my strategies weren't really the edge, I was. Which sounds arrogant, so I'll explain

A lot of people are dismissive of trading psychology (or sports psychology/performance psychology or whatever) but I'm a firm believer in the power of it. One thing all manual traders can't escape is themselves. Their fears, hopes, neuroticisms, ego etc etc. I believe we have to find a place of psychological balance to trade to the best of our abilities. Sure, there are also technical factors that are important in terms of entries, trade management and exits. But as soon as a trader clicks the buy or sell button they have some emotional investment in the outcome.

My advice to all traders who aren't yet where they want to be is to find a mentor, if at all possible. The benefits of the guidance and support an effective and reliable mentor can provide are numerous. If that isn't possible (they aren't easy to find), you have a couple of choices. Find a trading partner and support each other along the journey or, better still, become your own trading coach. I am my own trading coach, for better or worse.

One of the things I asked my students to do in the early days was to keep a trading journal and, in addition to their entries and exits, honestly record exactly how they felt during the trade. Some did this task, others didn't. But I believe those who did gained a huge benefit from doing so. Having to consciously check in with yourself during a trade and examine what your thoughts and feelings are, and then document them, is a process I heartily recommend.

A student who achieved funded trader status was someone who took this task very seriously. They gained an insight around their emotional triggers that no textbook could teach. Their dedication to their own development is first class. I don't have any doubts this person will achieve their dream, to make a living from trading.

Sorry, this has perhaps headed in a direction away from your original question  If you want recommendations of resources aimed at self-development I am happy to provide some. Where I can be of little help is recommending anything directly related to the technicalities of trading.

what i miss during this time i gain in fresh energy.

and at the latest when london closes, i turn off the screen and close the shop.

because i don't want to jeopardise my relationship with important people too much, so i keep everything in balance.

and i very rarely hold positions overnight because my sleep is important to me.

--- 帖子 #903 ---
Taking a bias from a longer timeframe and entering on a lower timeframe is fine. It can help with timing certainly.

I know I've said in the past (on Roadmap and here) that I prefer single timeframe analysis but that is only because there's a danger a trader can get overwhelmed by the different signals on each timeframe and lose their overall perspective. In your case, it looks like using both will be helpful.

--- 帖子 #904 ---
I agree about BE stops, I really dislike them.

One option you have is that you can choose to ignore long signals when they occur below your big moving average. The obvious downside to this approach is that you will potentially have bigger losers when a full reversal takes place, but on the plus side you won't get shaken out of positions.

Unfortunately everything is a trade-off. Whatever decisions we make have pros and cons.

Pending fxrabbi's reply, one thing you could consider on Laura's templates, is the amount of daylight at the time of the -50 cross.

On Tranqility's chart above:

First third of chart - down move. From the blue and red cross, look how long it took the red to cross the -50 and how little the daylight at that time.

Second two thirds of chart - up move. From the blue and red cross look how quickly the red then crossed the -50 and how much extra daylight.

--- 帖子 #914 ---
Hi Zimbinga.....

To have my #watchlist #Scanner #Screener ready.....I do/watch the followings:

1. Price Action Channel:

a.) I want to see the channel sloping and facing 2:00pm (long)/4:00pm (short) clock face.....this serves as my Strength meter.

b.) I want to see the channel become narrow......this serves as my Momentum meter.

2. Daylight:

a.) I takes only -50 levels cross.....this serves as my Strength meter.

b.) At the point of the cross I want to see a deep degree of separation between the blue line and the red line.....the wider the space the better for the momentum.....this serves as my Momentum meter.

c.) After the above have been met.......I pull the trigger.

Note:

I.) I am selective in my set-ups

ii.) I trade only H1.

iii.) I am one-timeframe trader.

Happy weekend

--- 帖子 #919 ---
FXRABBI and Others ----

When the trend is down but price has retraced to an area of resistance and we are looking for signs that the upward movement (pullback) has ended and the bearish trend will continue.Overall trend on the trading time frame is down:

The short-term trend on the trading time frame is up (has formed a pullback/retracement)

During the retracement, price retests a former area of price structure

Ideally, you’ll want for this pattern to form near the highs of the price structure.

Price may retest this area ''multiple times'' allowing for additional trading opportunities.

When price repeatedly retests a price structure (resistance) during a downtrend, it’s an indication that market makers are selling heavy volume in that area.

This allows for an ideal time to sell high (enter trade) along with the market makers and buy low (take profits).

Within Daylight system we can see the cross explains many ideas of what you should do and where you should stay out.

My chart posted,you all can see how the above occurred......if you look to the left,the action started before the area highlighted,the big picture is the idea of things. Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Hi scsstnt.......

My problem with multi-timeframe analysis.......is that I usually get lost in-between those timeframes.

As a trend trader..... just show me the trend added with volatility (strength + momentum)........I'm good to go.

As for S&R levels........I don't normally go far with that......All I do is ask myself these following questions:

I.) Are I'm in or close to a consolidation area.

ii.) How close I'm I to the previous high or low.

iii.) Are I'm getting close to a recent support or resistance levels....I look left.

Note: I do all the above in one timeframe....and I'm good to go.

I'm not surprised about you..... because I know where you're coming from......keep moving higher.

--- 帖子 #949 ---
Take all of that crap off of your charts. It will only delay and confuse what it is you are trying to accomplish here which is to become a CONSISTENTLY profitable trader.

You have everything you need right here in front of you.

This is my routine to find, enter and manage trades. Not saying it is the best method , however it is repeatable for me which is crucial in being consistent with your methods.

Step 1 always starts with a signal on the 1 hr for me. In my mind, it is really easy to move up and down from here according to your goals ( moving up and down is the next steps I am talking about)

I use my own method for the final screen. I look back to see if it has been at least 10 bars since we closed above/below the channel. This screen keeps me out of sideways markets MOST of the time. If I am shorting, I want the close below the channel to be the first close below in at least 10 bars and vice versa for longs.

-EDIT: Notice that you don't have to RUSH in as soon as you get the signal....watch and see what is happening before you jump.

It looks like this for me
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Once I have the signal, I move UP to the 4hr and Daily to see what a reasonable target is.

I got a target of 119.07 from the 4hr chart.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Step 2. Once I have my target, I move down to the 5 min to find an entry. This particular signal was given around the end of the NY session so I set a reminder to look at it closer to Asia open.

This was my entry off of the 5m chart about 30 mins before Asia open.
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

-EDIT2 :  Before anyone asks, I trail a stop a few pips beyond the opposite 1Hr channel as my stop since the signal was on the 1 hr.  For shorts I trail above the high channel line and for longs I trail below the bottom channel and then I try my level best to just simply leave it alone and see how it works out.

Thats it.....so very simple and repeatable. You don't need anything else to make money.

--- 帖子 #1075 ---
Yes and No. How do you quantify "less than the market had to give"   I am sorry to be blunt, however, that sentence doesn't make sense to me.

Do you expect to make every pip available? When you exit a trade you don't know what the next bars hold in store so you have every pip available to you at THAT POINT.  Looking at the chart later in the day and feeling like you left pips on the table is an exercise in futility. STOP doing that, it will lead you down a long and counter productive hole.

Why did you get out there?

Was it fear of losing your profits?

Was there a technical or "method" reason for the exit or was it just a fly by the seat of the pants type deal?

Lastly but the MOST IMPORTANT BY A MILLION MILES

Where did your PLAN say to exit. If you did not have a plan prior to entering the trade then you probably need to re read a lot of this thread.

Laura has presented several different exit methods across the 2 threads. I would suggest start with one and stick with it for at least a dozen trades and see what happens. No cheating, stick to the plan, win lose or draw

Let us know how it works out for you

He should read Laura's journal. Good section on physchology and a few exercises in discipline.

Yes, he needs to read all the threads after which, he will find most of his questions answered. And will not need to ask many more.

You need a point to get in and a reason to get out (levels etc) BUT you will NEVER take all available profit simply because you don't know, in advance, what the market will do. We make reasoned trades but the market is not a reason driven machine. Humans get in he way and emotions also. It is easy to spot a new or undisciplined trader: they seek to "improve" indicators; add more indicators and think indicators, algorithms etc are the way to profit. Think about it: if a plethora of indicators was all that was needed we would all be rich and the market frozen.YouTube is full of snake oil merchants selling dreams to the weak minded, greedy, or simply ignorant (in the nice sense). What I am trying to say is that your edge is "between your ears" and Laura's approach is your way into trading with an edge. Try her exercise , in her journal, of putting on a trade and letting price hit the other side of the channel before closing the trade. Yes -you will learn a lot about yourself. Remember, you can make good trades based on a reason or approach BUT many such trades will also lose because sh@t happens. But you keep going to let your edge work out.

You must realise that there are very few people like Laura who are willing to share with no expectation of financial reward. Therefore, I repeat, a close study of all her threads, and diligent application, will deliver its' own rewards ,to those willing study and test the given material in those threads.

--- 帖子 #1090 ---
Please see Lauras post above about stops. Stops are for emergencies....worst case possible, thats it.

Plans are made in advance and are based on what we "think" the market will do based on what we see. Whether it is "structure" or whatever we want to call it, we see and process the charts based on our experience. I don't make any excuses for losers after the fact.

I do this in order to make money. If I have money tied up in a position and that position is not making me money, then what good is it. Not only do I have the margin tied up, but I have to watch and babysit the position. Your stop and your exit are two entirely different things. Does that make sense?

I have trades that I enter on the daily chart. They are longer term positions (week or more) that have a stop but I will most likely exit all of them manually. Once again the stop is for emergencies.

Hope this helps

--- 帖子 #1092 ---
I'm glad this topic has come up.

It's perhaps no coincidence that brokers use the terminology 'stop loss' - I'd suggest giving it a different name in your heads, to frame things differently ... call it what it is: 'guaranteed loss'.

This isn't just semantics. If you take responsibility for managing your trades and close them out when price action deviates from your expectations, your guaranteed loss shouldn't come anywhere near to happening. I see more people losing due to bad stop placement than for any other reason.

One thing I tell my students is that the planning should take place BEFORE an entry is taken, not after you are in the position. You should have already played out the various possible scenarios in your head before pressing buy or sell. Then, when the market behaves in a certain way, you cannot possibly be surprised.

It's similar to what an elite sportsperson might do. Every possible scenario is played out in advance in their heads (and even in a physical sense in some cases), so that their muscle memory can kick in when reality starts to unfold.

--- 帖子 #1099 ---
Hi,

Let's say you are risking 1% of your account in the form of an emergency stop. Where you take profit has no relation to this. I know many will disagree with this statement but we can only ever take what the markets offer us. Also, you touched upon my views on RRR. I think it's meaningless, in isolation. Once we factor in our expectancy via our win rate, average winner, average loser and profit factor, we begin to form a more useful picture.

Remember, your emergency risk is 1% - not your expected risk. Your expected risk is where you intend to close the position if you are proved wrong in your theory. You should know in advance where this is likely to be as a worst case scenario. Actually, you might even end up with less risk as something might happen when the trade is open to make you want to get out early.

When calculating your position size and then your risk, look at where the emergency stop would be in relation to price action. Is it out of the way or is it in an obvious place where there are likely to be an accumulation of stops and pending orders sitting. Or, even worse, is it right in the middle of active structure. If it's the second or third options, you either want to pass up the trade or adjust your position size to allow a wider stop.

When calculating your profit target, you want to look at where a logical place might be for price to reach and potentially turn around. Personally, I have these targets in my mind but I wait to see how price reacts when it gets there. It might be that it sails right through the area and I can stay in the trade for a larger gain. Again, you might decide the logical profit target isn't large enough to justify the expected risk, in which case you move on to finding other opportunities.

I come at this from the viewpoint of someone who actively manages each trade. I don't do set and forget. If you are asking about a set and forget style of trading, I might struggle to give meaningful advice.

If you are also actively managing each trade, you can actually afford to be more generous with your emergency stop. Some traders go to 1.5%, some to 2%. But only because their stops are hit almost never.

I'm sorry I can't give a neat little "risk x% each trade and aim for y% profit" but my trading doesn't work on that basis.

Try to find entries where things are a lot more obvious.

I am new to the thread and found your Daylight strategy quite interesting. I read through all the posts in the last couple of days and am looking for some clarifications. If I consider the aggressive option, using the -50 bias approach, would I be right in entering a trade once the candle close closes outside the channel and the red line crosses the -50 line in the sub-window? Of course the closing outside the channel and crossing of the -50 line should be relevant to whether it is a buy or sell trade? If a daylight appears in the sub-window, but before the cross of the -50 line, do we need to wait till the -50 line is crossed?

Hope my question is clear.

Thanks

--- 帖子 #1220 ---

Lets call it a work in progress

--- 帖子 #1221 ---
Hi,

If you are using the -50 bias (regardless of whether you are using standard or aggressive), you first of all take your bias from the sub-window and then wait for price to close on the correct side of the channel.

If daylight appears in the sub-window before it crosses the -50 line you can take an entry but then you wouldn't be trading with the -50 bias.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1276 ---
These are my thoughts and opinions only and are based on what I see in the markets as a "daily cycle'

After the NY close at 5pm we are left with a couple of hours with wide spreads and no action or real movement as the day closes.

Once Asia opens, we start the daily cycle. We establish a range during the first couple of hours of Tokyo as the markets generally move in an orderly fashion with lower liquidity.

As we move towards the Frankfurt and London opens, volatility increases and we start to establish a "direction" for the day.

After we establish the opening range in Tokyo, I am on the lookout for the asian pairs that are near resistance or support and starting to establish a direction...whether it be continuation or reversal doesn't matter. This is where the "system" comes into play. Use the daylight method to enter as we try to get in early for the days move.

After the Frankfurt/London opening moves are done the market tends to consolidate before the NY open....not a good time or place to be trading....

Next we have the NY open. Highest volatility and liquidity of the day as both London and Frankie are on line as well. Good impulse moves here.

Next, NY goes into consolidation mode as London closes.

We are now back to approaching the afternoon and NY close and starting the cycle all over again.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)
